<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallatin_College">Gallatin College</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Gallatin College">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gallatin College is a two-year college for degree-seeking students and is housed on MSU campus to provide access to MSU campus student services including: dormitories, library facilities, and health services. As of May 2018,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Gallatin College offers six Associate of Applied Science degrees, five Certificates of Applied Science, a Professional Certificate in business management, Associate of Arts and Associate of Science transfer degrees, and a Developmental Education Program. It also offers a Dual Enrollment program for local high school students to broaden their available range of coursework offerings and share educational resources between MSU and local high schools.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>MSU houses approximately 4,200 students in its residence halls, approximately 70 percent of them freshmen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The university also offers housing to families and to graduate students<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Montana_State_Bobcats" title="Montana State Bobcats">Montana State Bobcats</a></div>
<p>The MSU athletic teams are nicknamed the <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">Bobcats</a>, and they participate in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> (I-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Championsip_Subdivision" title="Football Championsip Subdivision">FCS</a> for <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">football</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Sky_Conference" title="Big Sky Conference">Big Sky Conference</a>, of which Montana State University is a charter member. They field 13 varsity sports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>  Originally playing as the "Aggies," men's teams compete in football, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Track_and_field_athletics" title="Track and field athletics">track</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross-country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rodeo" title="Rodeo">rodeo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>. Women's teams include <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, basketball, track, cross-country, tennis, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, rodeo and skiing.
</p><p>Montana State University has won several national championships in men's <a href="/wiki/Rodeo" title="Rodeo">rodeo</a>, three national championships in football and one national championship in men's basketball. Non-varsity (club) sports include <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a>, men's <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">hockey</a>, men's <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a>, baseball, <a href="/wiki/Fencing" title="Fencing">fencing</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultimate_frisbee" title="Ultimate frisbee">ultimate frisbee</a>.  Montana State University has an ongoing <a href="/wiki/College_rivalry" title="College rivalry">rivalry</a> with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Montana" title="University of Montana">University of Montana</a>, most notably the cross-state football matchups, known as the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brawl_of_the_Wild" title="Brawl of the Wild">Brawl of the Wild</a>."
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Montana_State_Bobcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Montana State Bobcats men's basketball">Montana State Bobcats men's basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montana_State_Bobcats_women%27s_basketball" title="Montana State Bobcats women's basketball">Montana State Bobcats women's basketball</a></div>
<p>The school's basketball teams achieved fame throughout the 1920s by playing "racehorse basketball" and becoming one of the first schools in the nation to employ what is known as the fast break. Montana State College coach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ott_Romney" title="Ott Romney">Ott Romney</a>, who graduated with a Masters from MSC prior to World War I,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> pioneered the style of play, and by 1926 had assembled a team suited to playing an up-tempo brand of ball. <a href="/wiki/Cat_Thompson" title="Cat Thompson">Cat Thompson</a>, John "Brick" Breeden, Frank Ward, Val Glynn and Max Worthington were at the heart of the MSC team that won the Rocky Mountain Conference title three straight seasons, and bested <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utah_State" title="Utah State">Utah State</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BYU" title="BYU">BYU</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">University of Denver</a>. The 1928–29 team defeated the AAU Champion Cook's Painters in a two-of-three series, winning the Rocky Mountain Conference title. The team was named National Champions by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helms_Foundation" title="Helms Foundation">Helms Foundation</a>, which also named <a href="/wiki/Cat_Thompson" title="Cat Thompson">Cat Thompson</a> one of the five greatest players in the first half of the 20th century in college hoops.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Montana_State_Bobcats_football" title="Montana State Bobcats football">Montana State Bobcats football</a></div>
<p>In 1956 the Bobcats <a href="/wiki/List_of_college_athletic_programs_in_Montana" title="List of college athletic programs in Montana">football team</a> took a share of the NAIA championship in the Aluminum Bowl in Little Rock, Arkansas playing to a 0–0 tie with the Pumas of St. Joseph’s College from Rensselaer, Indiana. In 1976 the Bobcats of Montana State won a national football title in NCAA Division II at Wichita Falls, Texas beating the Zips of Akron, Ohio 24-13 in the title game. In 1984, the Bobcats returned to a national football title game played in Charleston, South Carolina, beating the Bulldogs of Louisiana Tech 19-6 for their third national football title. The MSU Bobcats football is the only college team with national titles in three different classifications. The team has won 20 conference titles and has made the NCAA FCS playoffs in 2010, 2011, 2012, and 2014.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rodeo">Rodeo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rodeo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For almost 30 years MSU hosted the College National Finals Rodeo. Bobcat Rodeo teams have won 8 national team titles, 32 individual national championships and multiple Big Sky Regional crowns. The Bobcats Rodeo team operates under the MSU Department of Student Affairs and is supported by the C.A.T. Rodeo Scholarship Association.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skiing">Skiing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Skiing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montana State Bobcats Alpine and Nordic Ski team compete in the Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Skiing Association and the NCAA Western Region and has produced 13 national champions. The Bobcat Nordic and Alpine ski program venues at Bridger Bowl and Bohart Ranch have hosted six NCAA National Championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Bill_Pullman" title="Bill Pullman">Bill Pullman</a>, Former Faculty Member, Actor (Honorary Degree, 2018)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Brautigan" title="Richard Brautigan">Richard Brautigan</a>, taught Creative Writing Spring, 1982<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Fonda" title="Peter Fonda">Peter Fonda</a>, taught Film Workshop, Fall, 2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_R._Horner" title="John R. Horner">Jack Horner</a>, former Regents Professor of Paleontology and Curator of Paleontology, <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Rockies" title="Museum of the Rockies">Museum of the Rockies</a>, taught Paleontology<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Markey" title="Patrick Markey">Patrick Markey</a>, taught as Adjunct Professor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Parkening" title="Christopher Parkening">Christopher Parkening</a>, Classical Guitarist (Honorary Doctorate 1983),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> teaches annual Master Guitar Class<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_M._Pirsig" title="Robert M. Pirsig">Robert Pirsig</a>, author of <a href="/wiki/Zen_and_the_Art_of_Motorcycle_Maintenance" title="Zen and the Art of Motorcycle Maintenance">Zen and the Art of Motorcycle Maintenance</a>, taught creative writing 1959–1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bill_Pullman" title="Bill Pullman">Bill Pullman</a>, taught Theater and active with <a class="external text" href="http://www2.montana.edu/shakespeare/" rel="nofollow">Montana Shakespeare in the Parks</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Quammen" title="David Quammen">David Quammen</a>, Science, Nature, and Travel Writer (Honorary Doctorate, 2000) taught and served as <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Stegner" title="Wallace Stegner">Wallace Stegner</a> Professor in Western American Studies, 2006–2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frances_Senska" title="Frances Senska">Frances Senska</a>, taught Ceramics Arts, 1946–1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gary_Strobel" title="Gary Strobel">Gary Strobel</a>, Microbiologist and Professor Emeritus of Plant Pathology, teaches Plant Sciences<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Associated Students of Montana State University is the student government of MSU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> It consists of an executive branch, senate, and judicial council. The executive branch is led by the student body president and vice president. In elections held in April 2018, students chose Taylor Blossom as president and Lizzy Thompson as vice president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The ASMSU Senate, in addition to addressing student concerns with bills and resolutions, allocates student fee dollars each spring semester. As of spring 2018, the body comprised 21 senators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> ASMSU's Judicial Council is made up of five students chosen by the university president and approved by the student senate. It reviews and interprets the senate's actions and reviews student appeals and election grievances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_groups">Student groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Student groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MSU's Office of Student Engagement organizes programs, events, and services for students. Its mission statement says the office "fosters meaningful engagement opportunities that challenge, support and empower students to be leaders on campus, in the community and beyond."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The office registers student clubs and organizations and currently has more than 300 listed groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraternities_and_sororities">Fraternities and sororities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montana_State_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Fraternities and sororities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2018, there are 7 fraternities and 4 sororities active at Montana State University.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The fraternities and govern themselves via a body known as the Interfraternity Council; a similar body, called the Panhellenic Council, exists for sororities. Both bodies focus on chapter development, scholarship, community service, member education, and alumni and public relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
